Spring and Autumn

Tidbits 170

— (Zheng Yimei)

The places where I work are all bustling places, such as theaters, film companies, one with constant singing and dancing, and the other with bright silver lights, reaching the extreme of sensuous and luxurious. Even the newspaper office where I used to work was full of beauties and constant music. However, I am as desolate as ever, still calm: because my state of mind is not shifted by the environment.

The beauty of sickliness, the Daiyu type, has been listed as something to be overthrown. Even the gentle and affectionate, quality Yu type, is not suitable for the times. It can be seen from the fact that modern women are fond of athletes.

Those who like to eat onions and chives call it fragrant, and those who don't like to eat it call it stinky. With the determination of food preferences, the definitions of fragrance and stink are established, so it is no wonder that there is no true right or wrong in the world.

Fruits often have the effect of treating diseases. For example, apples can treat dysentery, figs can treat hemorrhoids, mashing cherries into a paste and applying it to hands and feet can prevent chapped skin in winter, loquat leaves can treat coughs, lychee kernels and musk powder mixed with vinegar juice can treat ringworm, children eating small grapes can avoid smallpox, betel nuts can help digestion, sun-dried lotus root sections, after a cold year, decocting and drinking it can relieve chest congestion, bananas can relieve constipation, orange peels can resolve phlegm, olives can detoxify alcohol, roasted pears can treat chapped skin when washing the face with the hot water, accidentally swallowing a copper coin can be solved by eating water chestnuts, corn roots and leaves can treat urinary dribbling, hyacinth beans can stop vomiting, eggplant flowers can treat traumatic toothaches, peach blossoms can treat abdominal pain, and sugarcane can treat malaria.

Shanghainese use 弄 (lòng, lane) for 衖 (lòng, lane); for example, Hongmiao Lane is written as 虹廟弄, Xiangfen Lane is written as 香粉弄, and Xieqiao Lane is written as 斜橋弄. In fact, 衖 should be cut after 巷 (xiàng, alley), which is the same as 巷 (xiàng, alley), and should not be read as 弄 (nòng, do).

Four Foreign Suitcases 171

— Yang Yusheng

It is said that due to the devaluation of the US dollar, the number of Chinese students going to the United States for further study every summer is increasing year by year. Originally, studying is not a "capital-profit" business! Being able to reduce "costs" without affecting his title as a student abroad is really "getting a good deal"!

However, what do our compatriots bring back every year when they send a large amount of gold dollars to the United States? This loss-making account is difficult to calculate! If you must check this account, I have to honestly tell you: I don't know about other students abroad, but my friend Mr. X brought back four foreign suitcases!

That day, someone reported to me the news that he was coming to Shanghai from the United States, but because he was not an important person, it was said that no one was going to welcome him! Wasn't there a "grand occasion" when their large group of students went abroad two years ago! Now they are returning to their motherland dispiritedly, and no one pays attention to them. I think this may be because they are returning with loss-making account books! However, my friend Mr. X brought back four foreign suitcases! Even if it's a loss, it won't be "auctioned at the reserve price"!

A week after that day, he came to my house to see me. After I shook hands with him, I eagerly asked him if he had brought anything back. He sighed and said, "I brought four foreign suitcases to the motherland,——one suitcase is candies for the children to eat, one suitcase is clothes and utensils, one suitcase is Western books prepared to be displayed on Beijing Road, and one suitcase is full of dirty, torn shirts and socks!" Speaking of this, he laughed with emotion! But then he explained that the cost of washing a shirt in the United States was about the same as buying a new one, indicating the reason why his suitcase of dirty shirts and socks was piled up.

Finally, he said that although he had made considerable progress in his studies after studying hard in the United States for two years, he would feel the pain of unemployment at least temporarily when he returned to the motherland! I had nothing to say to comfort him. We talked about the most "fashionable" problems in Africa and Asia, and he got up and left. I mechanically sent him out the door, and I seemed to see four foreign suitcases in front of me!

Feather Fan 172

— Wu Yafei

Some time ago, I seemed to remember seeing Zhuge Liang in the Romance of the Three Kingdoms never leaving his feather fan. He was not afraid of the heat and needed it, just look at him holding it in his hand even in the coldest weather: then it can be known that his feather fan has other wonderful uses. However, similarly, Xu Maogong of the Tang Dynasty also had a fan, and Wu Yong in Water Margin also often had a feather fan in his hand, and even every military advisor used such a feather fan. So I think, perhaps they used this feather fan to help them use their thoughts and plan strategies: just as modern writers smoke, ancient writers loved to drink, which is the wonderful skill of the right wing.

However, the current feather fan is not exclusively used by military advisors, nor is it useful in winter, but it is used to dispel heat in summer.

This kind of feather fan is produced in Huzhou, Zhejiang Province. There are many feather fan shops there. They are like fur shops in Shanghai, but one specializes in winter business and the other only makes money in summer. After this season, they close their doors and wait for this time next year. Or, they may change to opening cotton shops in winter; therefore, cotton is used for winter business, while feather fans are used for summer, so this method is very suitable.

There are many kinds of feather fans, and the colors are gray, pure white, mottled, and red and green; however, red and green are dyed. The styles include Buddha's hand, chicken heart, round, flat head, and folding fan, and the price ranges from a few cents to more than ten dollars. The feathers are entirely from outside Tongmen, but they must be made in Huzhou to be famous, because it is said that the water under the Luotuo Bridge in Huzhou is phoenix water, so the feathers for making fans must be washed with water to be bright and soft. And it is said that this kind of feather fan can be used to remove wind, cold, evil heat, and other minor diseases.

Between Two Great Powers 173

Remains of Ma Chao Meeting Cao Cao at Tongguan 174

— (Ji Yijie)

Yesterday, Mr. Yang from the Northwest Training Office sent a letter informing us of the ancient relics of Cao Mengde meeting Ma Chao in Tongguan in the past. According to him: Tongguan was famous during the Three Kingdoms period. Ma Chao chased Cao Cao here. The pass is very dangerous, and it is true that one man guards the pass, and ten thousand men cannot pass. There is also an ancient relic, that is, on an ancient locust tree, there is Ma Chao's spear hole. It is said that Ma Chao chased Cao Cao to Tongguan, but failed to catch up. Ma Chao shot out a spear, which did not hit Cao's head, but hit the locust tree. Cao survived and later sealed the tree as a tree god. This locust tree is located in the Zhongfu Tianle shop on Dongdajie Street in Tongguan. The tree can be embraced by four people and is about fourteen feet high. Most of it is withered, but a small branch is still alive. There is a hole about a foot away from the ground, about one inch in diameter and one foot high, which is Ma Chao's spear hole. These are the remains of Cao Cao meeting Ma Chao in Tongguan, and so on.

Little Western Paradise 175

— Written by Zhang Henshui

Chapter Eighteen: Relatives of the Qi Faction Flatter and Grovel, A Petty Official Rebukes; A Ferocious Woman Creates a Great Disturbance, Annoying the Madam

The two runners chased to the stairs but couldn’t catch him, landing a kick on his shoulder. The accountant's body was already weakened from overwork, and this kick sent him tumbling and rolling down the stairs. Two waiters quickly helped him up. He looked around and saw dozens of travelers standing in the lobby. He sighed and shook his head twice. Two nosy travelers immediately asked him what had happened. The accountant stood in the middle of the lobby, looked at everyone, and said with a bitter smile, "I haven't offended any wealthy people. It's all because of you all not sleeping at such a late hour and making so much noise, which angered Madam Lan. I don't know whose family member was crying for a while, but Madam Lan said that if this traveler didn't stop crying, I should throw him out. You think we, who are in business, would dare to do that?" Everyone was in an uproar after hearing this. At this moment, the clerk, Qiu Zecheng, came down from upstairs and said to the accountant, "You are wrong. You were so rude to the madam just now, arguing with her at every turn. Now you are making reckless remarks in front of so many people." The accountant said, "I'm telling the truth. What did I say that wasn't true?" Zecheng said, "Madam Lan is still angry. Follow my advice, come upstairs with me, apologize to the madam, and it will be over." The accountant said, "Even if the travelers were noisy and disturbed the madam, it's not my fault. I've already been beaten and scolded. Why should I apologize?" Zecheng said sternly, "Don't you know? Earlier, a waiter went upstairs and was disrespectful to the madam. I personally heard you say that you used to work a minor official job and had seen all kinds of big shots. The madam said you looked down on the commissioner and insisted on sending you to the Public Security Bureau. I repeatedly pleaded for you, and she finally agreed to let you off if you bowed and apologized. Otherwise, she would call the police right away." Seeing Zecheng speaking calmly, the accountant naturally believed him and was stunned. But at that moment, someone in the crowd shouted "Hit him!" Immediately, everyone echoed, shouting "Hit him!" The commotion quickly escalated. (314)

Travels

Candle Creek Lake 176

— By Shufan

Yaojiang, the hometown of Wang Yangming, has beautiful mountains and rivers, second only to Kuaiji Creek. Mounts such as Kexing and Longquan have a constant stream of visitors, and many poems and essays celebrate their hidden beauty. However, the clear seclusion of the creeks and ponds and the strange beauty of the lake scenery are rarely mentioned. It's not that they are lacking, but because the place is remote and unknown, the water is used as a grazing area, isolated from the world.

The entire county has four lakes: Huangsha, Fuzi, Candle Creek, and Shanglin, with Candle Creek being particularly beautiful. It is located thirty miles northeast of the county, covering an area of over 14,000 acres, surrounded by mountains on three sides, a pristine scenic area! Take the Yuhu Highway bus to Henghe Town, get off the bus, and walk south for half an hour to reach it. Near the lake, the Siming Mountains are lush and dense, with no gaps in the sky. Following the winding green path, one suddenly emerges into an open space, revealing the clear lake, with reeds and rushes like clean brooms, sweeping through it. Ying Mountain cuts across the heart of the lake, appearing narrow and cramped. To the south, beyond Zhelu Forest, Guigang, and Yangmei Peak, the summit of Ying Mountain offers a panoramic view of the entire lake, without any hidden spots. Lion Ridge lies to the southwest, and looking east towards Xulang, wild chrysanthemums cover the mountainside like unmelted snow. Many small boats are on the lake, and fishing boats carry guests, the shadows of oars and the sounds of birds, the bamboo hats and the rustling trees, offering quiet pleasure in the midst of slight noise, making it impossible to fully describe its beauty! The sandbars emerge and disappear in the mist, like dragonflies skimming the water, with Ying Mountain seemingly about to swoop down and snatch them. According to historical records, the sandbar is the tomb of Sun Qinglian from the Tang Dynasty, and it is strange that it is not submerged even during high tides. The lake follows the foothills, making a large bend, with its western end deeply penetrating Xin'an, densely covered with sedges, and the misty peaks blending into one color. According to mountain farmers, many geese gather on the lake in winter, and people can catch five or six hundred in a day using nets, a benefit that cannot be rivaled; the richness of the aquatic products can be imagined. Descending the mountain, one can visit the tomb of Sun Zhonglie, named Sui, who lived at the same time as Wang Yangming and died in the disaster at Chenbin, as well as the tombs of his two filial sons, where the stone carvings of civil and military officials are well-preserved. The architecture of the previous dynasties is truly awe-inspiring. Walking through the dense shade, taking the road from Xulang, one can see thatched huts appearing and disappearing among the trees, terraced fields and ridges, and the sight of mountain people scolding oxen while plowing. All these scenes are worthy of artistic depiction! Xulang is the main peak surrounding the lake, and there is Yonggu Temple on the mountainside, suitable for cultivation and logging. The monks live a quiet life, without needing to seek connections with the outside world, resembling Tao Yuanming's Peach Blossom Spring, no less idyllic. Climbing further up, the sound of pines and streams create a unique harmony, with crows chiming in, making it a complete symphony of nature! There are ancient fir trees along the path, some with a circumference of over six spans, even more ancient and beautiful than those on the Tianzhang Road. The temple is not visible from below, but peering through the temple windows, one can see dozens of miles, as if the heavens opened up just for this view, leaving one in endless amazement! An old monk raises a fat ox, relying on each other for survival, creating a solitary sound in the valley, with no more than one or two visitors a year. Further up is Cuiping Temple, but due to the approaching dusk and the cold mist, we did not venture there. We spent the night in a farmer's house, drinking mountain wine, and slightly intoxicated, we surveyed the outdoors, seeing the bonfires by the lake shining brightly, reflecting on the waves, with colors like streamers. The people of Huangshan are still engaged in pottery. After two nights, we bid farewell to the host, with feelings of lingering affection that we couldn't suppress. I wrote a poem to commemorate the occasion:

Preparing weapons and raising cattle and sheep, this official land is abandoned and not yet filled, collecting pine needles at dusk to cook porridge with artemisia, the mountain home's hearth is also fragrant!

The mountain absorbs the dawn wind, turning into emerald waves, the water reflects the setting sun, wetting the rouge-like clouds, pitiful is the monk at Tiangu Temple's words: his white hair has no one to appreciate his good poems!

Begging for darkly brewed peach blossom wine, buying knife white fish for the ferry crossing, waking up not knowing what world this is? Mountain insects and branches of birds recite strange books.

Drunk, holding a sickle-shaped moon entering the south of the mountain, where to gather the secluded treasures hidden in winding paths? Cutting away the pine green, the clouds are white again, someone is filled with sorrow at Cuiping Temple!

Silently hiding my poems in my sleeves, I pass through the pine pass, feeling as free as clouds emerging from the mountains, accumulating clear coldness and startling April! Wild chrysanthemums are white all over Mount Xulang.

Amber moistens the moon setting in Mei'ao, emerald green stars scatter and reveal the sand, the old branches are twisted and ancient in the poems, the secluded charm of the lake is not related to flowers.

Records of Fragrant Haze 177

— Originally written by Princess Deling of the Qing Dynasty, translated by Qin Shouou

Now that the Empress Dowager was spending every day mingling with us young and beautiful court ladies, while it didn't necessarily spark any jealousy, the contrast inevitably made her feel that her own appearance was too old and haggard. So, she spared no effort in trying to preserve her fading beauty. Another thing she believed to be effective was human milk. Therefore, she had to drink more than half a bowl of human milk every day.

Since no one was giving birth in the palace, and no infants were being raised who were still being breastfed, where could they get this human milk every day?

It turned out that the Empress Dowager also had wet nurses! The Empress Dowager's wet nurses were carefully selected from the wives of those banner soldiers. They were naturally all young women who had just given birth. The selection was very cautious, with physical condition, appearance, and cleanliness being very important conditions. Sometimes, if they selected a particularly satisfactory woman whose appearance was also very beautiful, the Empress Dowager would definitely hire her for a long time and give her extra money so that she could hire another wet nurse to feed her own child. But this was very rare. Usually, they hired two or three at the same time, had them bring their children to live in the palace, and take turns squeezing milk out every morning for the Empress Dowager to drink. Once these wet nurses entered the palace, they were considered part of the Empress Dowager's attendants and were treated exceptionally well. The food they ate was exactly the same as what we ate. All utensils, clothing, and decorations were kept meticulously clean, as if they were guests coming to the palace. However, when squeezing milk every morning, the Empress Dowager still didn't dare to trust them and always had to send one of us to supervise. (414)

Wheat Research 179

— By Wang Weiyin

(1) The Significance of Studying Wheat: Clothing, food, housing, and transportation are the four essential elements of human life, and the food problem is especially important. Human life cannot exist without food and drink, so we must study how to obtain food. For thousands of years, our country has been an agricultural nation, with rice and wheat being the main agricultural products. However, due to the different climates in the north and south, the rice and wheat producing areas are different. Therefore, in the farmland south of the Yangtze River, rice is planted in nineteen out of twenty fields. The wheat planted is only used as a secondary product after the rice harvest, so farmers do not pay much attention to it. North of the Yangtze River, the land is higher and the climate is colder, which is suitable for wheat cultivation, so there are fewer farmers growing rice in the north. Therefore, northerners eat wheat and southerners eat rice, and what we should eat is wheat. In other words, wheat can almost represent the wheat family. Therefore, if we want to study the food problem, we must first study wheat.

(2) The History of Wheat: Humans discovered wheat long before recorded history. Some believe that the original origin was Mesopotamia, from where it gradually spread to various places, west to the Canary Islands, and east to our country. However, as the Book of Songs says, "Give me wheat for the coming year," then China's planting of wheat was already in the Stone Age, and it spread to the entire Eastern Hemisphere. As for the Western Hemisphere's knowledge of wheat, it began in the 16th century. Around 1530, Mexico began to import wheat, and in 1610, the British colonies in North America also tried to plant it.

(3) Wheat is Easy to Change Varieties: Wheat adapts to the environment very quickly. Its properties are easily affected by the soil properties, climate conditions, and mixing of varieties of the place of production. Therefore, the types of wheat are also becoming more and more diverse. Here is an example to illustrate this: In a certain place in England, although white wheat is often cultivated and sown in a farm, after several harvests, it can turn red. If this red wheat is planted on the slopes of the Pacific coast of the United States, it will turn into white wheat after several years, which shows how easily the properties of wheat can change.

(4) Wheat Production Areas: Most areas of the world can grow wheat, but the rate of reproduction varies. The temperate zone is the largest wheat producing area, and our country and the United States belong to it. Argentina and Australia account for one-eighth of the world's production and are the main producing areas in the tropics. However, wheat is also cultivated in the highlands of Peru, Bolivia, and Ecuador in South America. Parts of northern Canada, which were previously thought to be unsuitable for wheat cultivation, have also begun to be planted in recent years. The most difficult thing to plant in the far north is frost. In this period, crops such as wheat are safer.

(5) Wheat products, but the climate and geology are different everywhere, so there are areas harvesting wheat at any time of the year. The harvest season in Australia, New Zealand, Algeria, and Chile is January. The harvest season in certain areas of India and Upper Egypt is February and March. Syria, Persia, and other areas of India are in April. Algeria, Central Asia, and Northern Asia Minor are in May. Our country and Japan are in May and June. The states south of 40 degrees north latitude in the United States are in June. Northern United States, Southern Russia, France, and Hungary are in July. Eastern Canada, England, Germany, and the Netherlands are in August. Russia, Sweden, Norway, and Scotland are in September. Northern Russia and Finland are in October. Peru and South Africa are in November. South Australia and Burma are in November. From a global perspective, the total harvest in June, July, and August accounts for three-quarters of the total. This situation is very important for the world wheat market. The different harvest times can regulate wheat production in various places, and there is no fear of a shortage.

(6) Classification of Wheat: Wheat is usually classified into winter wheat and spring wheat. Botanists do not use this classification method, but it is quite common in commerce. Toincutn Saticum is the most common type of wheat. Other more common types include Emmcr, Spelt, Durum Wheat (a type of hard wheat), club wheat or squarehead wheat. Pirl wheat is another type. Millers must be very careful in choosing and preparing wheat, depending on the flour they want to produce. Stores also choose flour in the same way, depending on the type of food they want to make. Therefore, flour must meet the specific needs of consumers. The main types of wheat are listed in detail below: (1) Common wheat, cultivated all over the world; (2) Club wheat, produced most in the Pacific coast of the United States; (3) Durum wheat, produced in various countries, mostly in Russia; (4) Poulard Wheat, produced in Europe and America, cultivated more in Spain, Portugal, and Italy; (5) Mummy Wheat, produced less, slightly cultivated in Europe; (6) Polish wheat, mostly produced along the Mediterranean coast; (7) Indian dwarf wheat, mostly produced in India; (8) Small or one grained Spelt, produced in Europe, Germany, Switzerland, and Turkey; (9) Emmer or two grainde Spelt, produced in Europe and India; (10) Large spelt, produced in Europe, mostly in Germany. In addition, the commercial classification method can be divided into summer wheat and winter wheat according to the season of sowing and germination (as mentioned above), and can be divided into white wheat, yellow wheat, and red wheat according to the color of the wheat skin. White wheat and yellow wheat have less gluten and are suitable for milling. Or it can be divided into hard wheat and soft wheat according to the hardness and softness of the wheat. Soft wheat is exclusively used for milling raw materials. (See "Recent Advanced Commodities" by Japanese, Itaguchi Takenosuke)

(7) The Uses of Wheat: Wheat is of good quality, rich in nutrients, and suitable for making noodles, dumplings, and bread. Therefore, flour products are more numerous than those made from any other grain flour. The demand for wheat from emerging manufacturers of breakfast foods is also increasing. Several decades ago, corn flour, rice, and oat flour, which were made in various ways, were the most important of our food, and have now entered the era of packaged food, so in addition to oats, large quantities of wheat, rye, barley, and rice are needed. Before this kind of food is packaged, it is steamed, boiled, or pickled by using a festival or it has become wheat essence and glucose after fermenting and pickling, so that it can be digested more easily, and there is no cooking process when it is taken. This is also one of the proofs of modern food progress, but research is not a one-day or two-day effort. Among the artificially manufactured foods of modern times, grain flakes made by rolling are first-class. The manufacturing method is to steam the hulled grains and roll them into thin flakes with rollers before they are dry. They can be put on the market after they are dry. This kind of food, the imported oatmeal currently sold on the market, is one of them, and the annual import quantity is not small. The natives in certain places in Southern Europe are accustomed to eating pasta and similar foods, but the consumption of this kind of food has now spread to other countries, and the manufacturing industry needs to use special wheat. Ordinary hard spring wheat or einkorn is not suitable. Manufacturers in the United States usually use Durum Wheat as raw material. The amount of wheat suitable for making pasta is found in Durum near the vicinity of Yafu in Italy, Algeria, and Russia and Poland in Southern Europe. Because the above wheat contains gluten, it is a valuable raw material for making pasta.

(8) The Future of Wheat Planting: During the Great War, all the participating countries, due to food shortages, made every effort to save flour and mix part of potatoes and corn to make flour. In the future, if it is necessary to reduce the consumption of wheat, this kind of substitute may be used for relief: but in terms of the various cooking uses of wheat, there seems to be no suitable substitute, because the biggest difference between wheat and other grains is that the gluten of wheat contains two kinds of proteins, one is Gliadjd and the other is Glnlenin, so it is a suitable material for making noodles. Whether other grains have these two proteins is not confirmed. Now, although the world's population continues to increase, the number of people eating wheat is increasing day by day compared with those who eat rye and corn. However, from the recent outlook for the future, there is no sign that we must save the consumption of wheat. One of the most noteworthy things about wheat production is that the supply of wheat worldwide mostly comes from countries with low yields per acre. This is because the planting of wheat has recently changed from manual labor to mechanized labor. Most wheat growers use large-scale machinery to cultivate on poorer land, but the main reason is that most of the world's wheat is still from crude cultivation systems. Intensive cultivation systems will increase the value of wheat production, which can be proved by the high productivity of a few European countries. This kind of production method seems to require higher costs and slightly higher prices to offset the various costs of producers. However, our production economic methods are not limited to this. Carefully selecting seeds, improving the organization of farm work, and more effective cooperation among producers in cultivation, harvesting, and selling crops can all increase the economic efficiency of crop production. If we want to reduce consumption and make the current wheat production supply more people to eat, it is impossible in reality.

But there is one thing that can be done, that is, to increase the world's cultivated area. In most areas of Western Europe, it seems that the maximum amount has been reached in terms of cultivated area and harvest. There is also no possibility of a large increase in the area of wheat cultivation in the United States; but by promoting the planting of arid crops with irrigation and drainage, and planting wheat on barren old fields, etc., it is still possible to open up a large number of wheat-producing acres in the United States. The expansion of other parts of the world is also enough to increase the wheat production area. The temperate zone of South America has a very large area that has not been opened up, and is mostly used for animal husbandry. Both Genggai and Paraguay also have land to be opened up for wheat cultivation. In the future, the vast land of Canada and the three parts of East, North, and South Africa will all be major wheat-growing areas. The output in our country and parts of Siberia may also gradually increase. If the irrigation method can be used, the number of acres of wheat production in Australia can also be increased. In short, the world's wheat production capacity will eventually be higher than it is now. As for the improvement of seeds and the invention of machinery, it is enough to make the output increase day by day. If we stick to the old methods and do not know how to improve, even if we do not encounter water and drought disasters and the population increases sharply, and the output is fixed, it can be inferred that in the future, there will be a day when food is not enough to be distributed. We, the citizens of a country that is called an agricultural country, should pay more attention to this.

Free Talk

Writing About a Typical Figure 180

— Qu Yi

The so-called typical figure is not a special figure. On the contrary, it is a very ordinary and commonly seen figure. In real society, such a figure is often forgotten and not remembered because they are too ordinary and too commonly seen. On the other hand, they do possess all the characteristics of the social stratum to which they belong. However, once written about and discussed by people from the same or different social strata, they suddenly realize that this book contains a true reflection of themselves or someone they commonly see. This is a writing method in which the author abstracts from real society and concretizes it as a conclusion. Let's tentatively call this writing method "inductive." Lu Xun's Ah Q is an example. When "The True Story of Ah Q" was published, it caused a sensation in Chinese society. Among the readers with peasant characteristics, they suddenly saw such a figure that had long been forgotten.

However, social phenomena are constantly changing, and in extremely complex ways. At first glance, it seems like a kaleidoscope, with unfathomable depths. But upon closer observation, each phenomenon is not only interconnected and inseparable but also moves in the same direction, either declining or rising, for the same purpose. A genius writer can grasp the inevitability of its development in the dynamics of this phenomenon and mold a character with a potentially developing personality. When this figure is presented to the current real society, the reader may see a special figure, making them disbelieve that such a figure could exist in the world. But as time passes, under the inevitable laws, the conditions that made people doubt the existence of this figure are eliminated. This molded figure becomes more and more vivid, and finally, the real society is filled with real figures identical to the molded one. Then, people wake up as if from a dream and cannot help but exclaim, "There really is such a person!" The typicality of this molded figure is further expanded. Let's tentatively call this writing method "deductive." Turgenev's Bazarov is an example. The appearance of Bazarov greatly dissatisfied the Russian society at the time, as they believed that such a figure did not exist in society. However, years later, facts proved Bazarov's existence. The appearance of Bazarov was Turgenev exploring the general character of the Russian intellectual class at the time, finding its development direction, and giving it form.

What we have said above about the "inductive" and "deductive" writing methods only describes the formation process of the figure. It does not encompass the entire speculative process of the writer when creating the figure. The speculative process of a writer when creating a figure is very complex. They must expand the scope of speculation to the entire society, or at least understand the society in which this typical figure emerges. This depends on the writer's own level of practice in reality, and it is not just a matter of speculation.

We do not want to elaborate on this here. But regardless of the figure's formation process, the writer must accomplish a major task when creating a typical figure: that is, to try to omit unnecessary elaborations and make the figure stand out as much as possible. In other words, to write a typical figure, the writer must have a large group of unwritten figures in mind as a contrast to this typical figure, making the character of this typical figure very clear.

Recently, I saw a short story by Chekhov titled "A Peculiar Man." In reality, the person depicted by Chekhov is not a peculiar person but a typical person. The story is very simple; it is about a gentleman named Guoyaf who goes to the midwife Maya to ask her to deliver his wife, introducing himself very seriously.

"I am an assistant teacher at a vocational school. My name is Guoyaf. I am asking you to deliver my wife. Please hurry."

Sure enough, the midwife quickly prepared to leave. He then said that the price should be agreed upon first. The midwife said it was fine to give whatever he wanted. However, he looked at the midwife coldly and firmly and said a lot: "No, I don't like that way. It's best to agree on the value first. I don't want to take advantage of you, and you don't want to take advantage of me. We should agree on the price first to avoid trouble later." He also said: "I work myself and respect other people's work. I don't like being harsh to people. I don't want to give you too little, and if you want too much, I will ask how much the market price is." So the two began to discuss the price. He would only offer two rubles, but the midwife did not agree. He simply ran out and did not ask her to go. However, half an hour later, he finally came back, offered three rubles, asked her to go, and added, "After the price is agreed upon, no additional money is allowed." However, when the midwife arrived at the house, delivered the baby, and congratulated him, saying, "It's done, thank God, there is another person in the world!" At that time, he still maintained a heartless, blank expression and said, "Very good. However, conversely, more sons also cost more money. A child is born only to wear clothes and eat!" This made the midwife tremble when she saw him. Finally, she saw him standing in front of her son, who was reading in elementary school, calmly saying: "You know how to drink, you should also know how to work. You just swallowed a mouthful, but you didn't think about how much a mouthful is worth. It's not earned by working. You should think about it while you eat..." This scared the midwife so much that she didn't dare to take the money and ran away...

In this short story of less than three thousand words, the writing is very economical. It can be said that there is not a single careless stroke, and every stroke is focused on molding Guoyaf's character: the character of a gentleman with a merchant's temperament. Although this is a Russian figure, a person who calculates every ounce is also commonly seen in Chinese society. This makes him a typical figure.

However, in writing about typical figures, it is easiest to turn into writing about psychological figures. That is, to develop the particularity abstracted from the universality of the figure as much as possible, even isolating this particularity and writing it as a truly peculiar person (such as the figures that appear in "Investiture of the Gods". Those cannot be regarded as typical figures but as "monsters"). The consequence is that the reader's likes and dislikes of the figures in the work become personal likes and dislikes, forgetting the social origins of the typical figure. The social value of art loses its existence here and makes the work something like a personal attack. Therefore, here, writing about typical figures still relies on the discovery of the sociology of personality. And the discovery of the sociology of personality must pay attention to the following two points: the socialization of personality and the reflection of the universality of particularity.

Jishi Dance 181

Mid-Autumn Festival Four Years Ago 182

— He Wei

The Mid-Autumn Festival has passed. In this autumn when the west wind is rising and the grass and trees are about to wither, some sentimental poets may again come up with a set of mournful chants like "Hearing more maple leaves fall, the sound of autumn drips." In the long autumn night, I am afraid they will rise up with the sigh of "Tossing and turning, unable to sleep, putting on clothes and wandering"?

The Mid-Autumn Festival is a good festival for revelry, but it is also a day that makes people melancholy and sentimental. The so-called mood of "Raising your head to look at the bright moon, lowering your head to think of your hometown" is particularly prominent during this full moon. In the past, whenever I encountered this festival, I would always sadly think of my hometown. The scene of the whole family relying on the trees to enjoy the moon on the slope behind the village in my childhood made me feel extraordinarily lonely.

But now I no longer have this feeling. The urgency of life and the commotion of national affairs have alienated me from my hometown and diluted my attachment and nostalgia for my hometown. So this year's Mid-Autumn Festival, I was silent and did not complain or feel any emotion.

But I kept thinking about the Mid-Autumn Festival four years ago. Like a ghost possessing me, I think of that memorable, tragic, and great day every day.

The Mid-Autumn Festival four years ago, yes, the Mid-Autumn Festival four years ago! Many people may have forgotten that memorable day, right? But at that time, it did cause a huge wave. Everywhere you could hear impassioned speeches, and you could see actions that defied death at any time. Although the mountains and passes were so insurmountable, separated by layers, the "flocks of wild geese flying towards the Han Pass," their wailing, made the people of the whole country boil with enthusiasm, and their emotions were high. The calls to "reclaim the old mountains and rivers from the beginning" and shed blood outside the Great Wall merged into a greatest march, shaking everyone's soul and burning everyone's enthusiasm.

This memorable day - the Mid-Autumn Festival four years ago has passed for four years, and people are probably enjoying the joy of singing and dancing in peace. How can they still think of the scene at that time!

This is Shanghai (Part 2) 183

— Dongli

"Please come in."

The medical doctor speaks Chinese very well.

Two women, one slender and snake-like walking in front, the other short and plump behind. Needless to say, they are dressed very luxuriously, their faces are covered with a layer of powder, their hair is permed, and they are wearing long earrings, just like the typical concubines in Shanghai.

"Good evening, Mr. Gu ××××."

The two women said together with a smile, speaking in English, the short and plump woman's voice slightly heavier.

The things after the meeting need not be described in detail. As usual, the doctor led one of his clients into the inner room, took off her clothes, and performed his duty of giving her an injection. After finishing one, he gave the second person an injection. While giving the injection, the doctor asked the client if her symptoms had improved in the past few days. If the female client shook her head, he would flash a charming look, smile, and although he did not say anything, he was implying, "Who told you not to listen to me and still do that good thing with your lover?" When the female clients denied his implication, he would not hesitate to say:

"Then, I'm telling you, give four more injections in a row, and I guarantee it will be cured!"

"As long as it's cured, I'm not afraid to spend money!" It was precisely because he saw through this that the doctor deliberately increased the price of the injection from the original three or four yuan to such a large amount as one hundred yuan. The injection fee is expensive, but that doesn't matter. The rich can spend money, and their unconcerned attitude towards spending money is just like the poor who take their own strength for granted. What's more, this doctor with medical degrees from two countries really did cure some of his clients' illnesses. However, no matter how many he cured, there were still many people getting infected. If you want to ask, "Why are so many people getting 'venereal diseases'?" It's better to ask "Why are there so many concubines in China!" These are both questions that no one can answer. Now, the doctor has finished giving injections to these two customers, and then three or four more brightly dressed women walked in.

What a great business! However, since there is no sign nailed outside the building and no advertisements have been placed in the newspaper, how can there be so many patients seeking treatment! The effectiveness of word-of-mouth transmission is probably no less than that of paid advertisements in newspapers. The doctor saw this clearly, so he often urged his female clients:

"Introduce a few more to me. You know a lot of people."

Most of the people they know are concubines like them, and many of their peers have the same symptoms. Just think, if a man has four or five women, he will inevitably be unable to take care of them all. Can you blame the women for secretly finding other ways out? Can they avoid getting "venereal diseases"? Since they can ask for more money from men, they will naturally come here for treatment. This Derby medical doctor is simply having good luck.

However, do you really think this Derby medical doctor is the real deal? Wrong. Not only is he not a medical doctor from Derby, but he is not even qualified to be a "bachelor"! He only fooled around in a local secondary medical school in his hometown, and later worked as an assistant in a small local hospital for a year. After that, he stayed at home for five years, and in the sixth year, he came to Shanghai on a presidential ship.

"It's easy to make money in Shanghai, and it's even more profitable to practice medicine. Rich Chinese people are superstitious about foreign doctors!"

Thanks to an uncle who came back to his hometown from Shanghai and told him this way to make money, he came to Shanghai to seek a living. Now he has really made a fortune. His uncle's words were not false, because stubborn female clients often scolded those Chinese Western doctors in front of him for being half-baked and incompetent.

This night, until twelve o'clock, the doctor treated a total of thirteen female clients for venereal diseases.

The Singer on the Sea 184

— Dabao

The ocean is my cradle,

I grow up on the sea.

Facing the sun, looking at the sky, listening to the raging wind and waves,

This is my habit:

A deep, broad, floating cradle,

Nurturing my unruly personality.

I praise the straits, the torrents and mountains...

The ebb and flow of the autumn tide,

And the light of the vast night;

I praise the noisy docks,

And the glorious harbors.

Life is an endless float,

--I am not tired;

I despise mediocrity and conservatism,

Praise the opening up to nature,

And the constant torrent of the world.

I do not cling to my old home and relatives either,

On the other side of the ocean, there are also our partners and destinations.

Dream (Two) 185

— Zang Kejia

"How wonderful it would be to have Xiaocui by my side."

In the terrifying atmosphere, she suddenly thought of Xiaocui. This girl was a companion when she was at home. Although she couldn't do much heavy work, she could pick grass in the graveyard and help add firewood to the stove. Even if she didn't do any work, it would be good. A fourteen or fifteen-year-old child, running around and playing with a puppy (she couldn't find other companions nearby), sometimes picking a string of poplar catkins or some wildflowers and pinning them on her black braids, turning her face to admire herself for a while before jumping to her mother and pulling her, saying it was good. In the spring, she picked up a small bird learning to fly that had fallen down and raised it, like a mother caressing a child, raising it until it could fly, and then teaching it some tricks. She and the puppy chased each other year-round in these graves. She found this independent world very lovely. In the spring, flowers of various colors bloomed in the graves, and she picked them and sat on the ground pressing the thick snow, their hearts indescribably bright.

"Xiaocui is a child in the embrace of nature."

Sister-in-law Wang Er wouldn't say this sentence, but she did have this meaning. When Xiaocui's father was away, she would sit beside her mother with a smile on her face and say, "Mom, I love you," and then use her right hand to bend down the thumb of her left hand, "I also love Grandpa," bending down the first finger. "I also love Xiaohei" (she always called the puppy that), and the third finger also fell down. Finally, she leaned coquettishly into her mother's arms and said, "Mom, let's four of us be together for the rest of our lives."

Xiaohei burst open the split bamboo door and came in, covered in grass leaves. She suddenly woke up from her daytime dream. Xiaohei walked up to her and shivered, the grass splashing around, and it lay down leaning against its mistress's leg, wagging its tail uncontrollably, humming and making loving sounds.

Fear no longer existed in Sister-in-law Wang Er's heart at this time. But sadness filled that emptiness. Xiaocui was still guarding her last year, but this year, alas, she looked at the puppy and tears almost fell. Xiaohei raised its head as if it were also remembering something.

Sister-in-law Wang Er said that she was a pitiful person. She followed Wang Er in her twenties, leaving only a debt, and now she is over forty years old, with nothing else to hope for. It would be good if she had raised a daughter, but she had been sold by her hateful husband last year. She was sold as a concubine to Li Er, the young master of the flower country. Because of this, the couple had argued countless times, and had even fought a few times, but the husband is heaven, and what strength can overcome heaven? Moreover, the husband had a good reason. He said that a daughter could not start a family anyway, and would have to marry sooner or later. Li Er was a shopkeeper (note) with power and influence, and the lives of our whole family were in his hands. Last year, during the Cold Food Festival, the second young master came to add soil, and Xiaocui, who was watching the burning of paper money to the gods next to him, was picked on by the second young master, who was determined to make her his concubine. Sister-in-law Wang Er heard this and refused to die, firstly because the child was small and she couldn't bear to part with her, and secondly because everyone knew how fierce Li Er's wife was, and besides, there were a large family of old and young in Li Er's family, and Xiaocui, a widowed girl, couldn't support them. But the husband didn't think so. He said that since the young master had taken a fancy to her, there was no way, and besides, he could get a hundred silver dollars. He planned to tell Sister-in-law Wang Er to use this hundred dollars to buy an acre of land to plant, and save the grain, and then buy a calf, and hire a child to let it graze, and at the same time, it could help with the work. The husband's plan was very thorough, as if as long as Xiaocui was sold, the long-term plan could be settled. Sister-in-law Wu Er was speechless after being told by her husband at night, but when she saw Xiaocui's lively appearance the next morning, she immediately changed her mind again.

The husband is heaven, and what strength can overcome heaven?

Xiaocui was finally carried away by a sedan chair from the Li family. One hundred dollars also became an acre of land.

However, this was not what the husband had planned. Not long after an acre of land was bought, it was surveyed by the automobile committee, and a white lime was sprinkled from the center without being crooked. The couple were so upset by this white lime that they didn't eat for many days. Sometimes, Wang Er suddenly woke up in the middle of the night and cried out, and when Sister-in-law Wang Er woke up in shock and asked him repeatedly, he just stared straight with both eyes, and it took a long time to catch his breath, "Oh, a car crushed Xiaocui!"

Supplement to the Shanghai Newspaper

Talk

On Beauties 186

— Gu

The terms "standard beauty" and "model beauty" are really novel and elegant, but I really don't understand the meaning of these two terms. Standard, is it like a standard clock, standard cigarettes, etc.? Model, is it like a model factory, model prison, etc.? If so, then all women must be born exactly like them to be called beauties, otherwise, no matter how charming and beautiful you are, you cannot be called a beauty. Suppose you want to raise a pretty daughter, you must pre-make such a model.

The ancients had imagined an ideal beauty, saying that adding an inch would be too long, reducing an inch would be too short, applying rouge would be too red, and applying powder would be too white. It was moderate in length and short, and the fat and thin were appropriate, but he was only imagining and fabricating. To this day, no such standard and model beauty has appeared. Even the beauties called by the ancients were not exactly the same in size, length, black and white, fat and thin, so who is the standard, and who is not the standard? Who is the model, and who is not the model?

Women only have beauty and ugliness, there is no standard or model. Moreover, the meanings of standard and model are originally the same, but the faces of standard beauties and model beauties are definitely not the same, so who is the standard and who is the model? Only heaven knows. The ancients said, "Beauty is in the eye of the beholder," and also said, "Other people's wives are better." These words are originally biased towards emotions, but the viewpoint in the eyes of a lover and the viewpoint in the eyes of a non-lover are ultimately different. So are the so-called standards and models all the tone of lovers?

In today's world of eroticism, everyone has forgotten the country's shame and misfortune, and are desperately supporting the beauty's scene, hoping to win the beauty's frown and smile and spiritual pleasure. Therefore, school beauties, dance queens, flower country presidents, socialites, Shanghai Misses, etc., appear like fleeting spring clouds. Now these terms are also felt to be old-fashioned or outdated, so the terms standard beauty and model beauty have emerged in response to the times. I have nothing to say, I can only admire the Chinese people's intelligence.

Sketch of Beiping 187

— Meng Hua

(3) Water Carriers

Even on cold winter mornings, one can see many water carriers in every alleyway, pushing their heavy water carts. People curled up in warm quilts feel even colder when they hear the "Yi-ya, Yi-ai" sounds.

Every few alleys, there is a dilapidated house where a well occupies almost half of the space. The water drawn up by the pulley is poured into a trough beside the well. The water drawers and carters are all tall Shandong men.

Whether it is a cloudy day or a day with wind and sand, they brave the wind, bending their backs, using all their strength, stepping firmly, and laboriously pushing the carts. The hutongs of Beiping were originally like incense burners; when it rained, thawed, or snow melted, a half-foot of mud accumulated. The wheelbarrows often sank deeply into the mud, and even if those men strained their temples, they could not push them more than two or three steps. When you see a water carrier and his son on the street, one pulling in front and the other pushing behind, veins bulging, noses running, and stinking sweat pouring, it immediately reminds you of those mules struggling in the mire. What is the difference between their lives and theirs?

(4) Tianqiao (The Heavenly Bridge)

Tianqiao is the hell of the propertied and the paradise of the propertyless.

There are no high thresholds here. I cannot see ladies and wives decked out in finery, or young masters with slicked hair and powdered faces. I cannot see cars or smell perfume. But from morning onwards, many people rush here from all directions to seek their entertainment and pick up cheap goods.

On both sides of the road are small shops selling old stalls and old clothes. The clerks also perk up when they see you, using touching words to deal with you. "Want a gown? Want long trousers? Whatever you want, please come inside and take a look..." These are all good things, and the prices are very fair. As soon as one finishes speaking, the other interjects. The people who pick the items bargain prices. Village girls are touching the satin shoes with red flowers on the shoe stalls, with their heads held low.

In an extremely large earthen field, people have formed countless circles, and the smell of sweat assaults everyone's noses. On this side and that side, thousands of different voices rise up all the time, and the sellers have to shout at the top of their lungs. The sellers are mostly good men, and most of them have some skills. Those who wrestle sell their strength, and those who kick shuttlecocks and spin tops sell the flexible skills they have practiced for many years. Blood and sweat are their capital. Because of this, this job is also very difficult to earn a living. When they are playing energetically, they are very enthusiastic in cheering and clapping, "Damn, this kid!" They praise him like this with a smile. But when it's almost over, the clever people run away, and after bowing, there are only a few scattered copper coins on the ground.

When walking past the thatched sheds, you can always hear a burst of "Ai!... Cough... Dong... Dong... Dong... Yi Dong... Yi Dong..." This is the sound of singing "Dagushu" (a form of storytelling accompanied by drum). They are all young girls, or those who have lost their support, with a small handkerchief clipped between their fingers, forcing their thousand-pound eyelids open, straightening their voices, and singing from morning to noon, from noon to evening, to earn two or three hundred copper coins.

There are things to eat, things to play, and also so-called dental hospitals. In front of this "hospital," there is a square table with two glass bottles filled with yellow teeth. There are often many people seeking medical treatment inside the shop. Next to the hospital is a fortune-telling shop (there are so many fortune-telling shops in Tianqiao that it is really impossible to count them!). The "Free Palm Reading" slip is pressed under the stationery tube on the table, and business is quite good. Moreover, when talking to people from the countryside, they also show the unique attitude of a "prophet." The dentists have pliers, and the fortune-tellers have mouths. Everyone relies on their respective magic weapons to maintain their lives, but only heaven knows their skills.

This is their entertainment, their everything, their paradise!

Is this their entertainment, their everything, their paradise?

Random Notes by the River 188

— Yang Zhongshuo

(1) Boat

Originally, my body was a little sick, and my spirit was stimulated, so I woke up before dawn. I crawled out of bed and sat on the edge of the bed, staring blankly at the pitch-black sky, without a single star. The weather was very cool, with a hint of autumn. The rustling sound hurt my ears very badly. It turned out that it was raining, and it had been raining for several days. This lingering rain aggravated the depression in my heart.

At five o'clock, the sky outside the glass window gradually brightened. Dark clouds and thick fog were blown by the autumn wind to the south and moved a lot. The sound of soybean-sized raindrops hitting the roof tiles was like the weeping of a woman who had been wronged.

The sky was getting bigger. I rubbed my distracted eyes with my right hand and stood up from the edge of the bed and walked to the window. My body was almost shivering from the cold air in the morning. Reciting the lines "Autumn wind and autumn rain are so sad," I felt as if I had left reality and fallen into another illusory environment.

When my consciousness returned to its original state, I realized that my eyes were fixed on a sailing boat with a dark color and dilapidated masts on the river. The boat was going against the current, and several boatmen were inserting their poles into the water with all their might, trying hard to support it. At this time, my sight shifted to the shore, where three or four naked boatmen were pulling a rope with all their might. Those bodies, tanned black by the sunlight in June, aroused my envy. That solid, strong cured meat, and the fresh and obvious outlines all showed their spirit of fighting for survival.

(2) Pagoda

On the bank of the rapid river, there stands a pagoda that soars into the clouds and has a very strong medieval magical atmosphere. The pagoda was originally very high, but because it was built on top of a hill, it appeared even more majestic and arrogant. It is said that this pagoda has a history of more than a thousand years. Because the days are long, the beams, pillars, bricks, and tiles are inevitably moldy and rotten. Moreover, after the tourists climb and trample on it every spring and autumn, it becomes even more dangerous. Therefore, the local gentry all advocated that it must be repaired. Their superficial reason is that this pagoda has historical value and is famous in the country. But according to people familiar with the inside story, the main reason for repairing this pagoda is the turbulent river that is making trouble. "When the pagoda collapses, the river overflows," this is their unchanging theorem. The original intention of building the pagoda was to suppress the river god and make him lose his ability to make waves. Embankments can be ignored, but the pagoda cannot be repaired. This is also not surprising. The Chinese nation has such a deep concept of its ancestors that the cause created by the ancestors must be preserved, and the ancestral precepts must be followed. The pagoda was built by the ancestors, and it was also the ancestors who said that it should be used to suppress the river god.

Now, this repaired pagoda is even more magnificent, with painted beams and carved buildings, and gold and jade shining brightly, making it even more magnificent. However, since the pagoda was repaired, I have not often gone to that hill. I always feel that the strong smell of paint makes my breathing uncomfortable. When the weather is clear, I dare not even look at the gilded top of the pagoda, because the reflection of the sunlight will make my eyes feel strangely painful.

I remember that before the pagoda was repaired, I would quietly walk up the hill and into the pagoda after school every day. The abbot of the monastery next to the pagoda was too clever. He placed many mahogany tables and a dozen earthen rattan mats in the corridor. Whenever I came, the old man who made tea would bring a pot of hot Longjing tea. I would lie on the mat, take a sip of hot tea, rest for a while, unfold the book I brought, and read it slowly. When I saw something good, I would really clap my hands and applaud. When I was tired of reading, I might as well get up and pace back and forth, say happy words, and also look at the poems written by anonymous poets on the walls. Seeing that the sky was getting dark, the bell in the ancient temple issued an order to leave, and after paying for the tea, I quietly left the pagoda and went down the hill alone.

This kind of leisurely life was brutally deprived by those gentry who advocated repairing the pagoda to suppress the river and save the people. For a year, my heart seemed to have lost something, and it was extremely empty.

Standing in front of the pagoda, I sighed, feeling very depressed. Thinking of the past, I couldn't help but feel that all the past events were like drifting in the wind.

Ramblings from an Autumn Window 189

— A Pure Child

I have loved sweets since I was a child, and now I am not yet thirty, but my mouth is full of cavities; but I still love sweets as much as ever. Half of this habit was formed because my grandmother spoiled me too much. She was fifty years old when she saw her grandson. Father sometimes saw that I was too indulgent and said to Grandmother with a smile, "This child will be spoiled by you." But Grandmother's reply was, "Why don't you have a few more children?"

As long as a child has someone to support him, he will do whatever he wants without any scruples. There are three osmanthus trees in my yard, and during the Mid-Autumn Festival, the whole yard is fragrant. It seemed to be the cook in my house who tricked me into thinking that osmanthus flowers tasted sweet. One day, I actually climbed a ladder to pick osmanthus flowers. Fortunately, I didn't cause any trouble, but I tasted the bitter flowers and twisted my grandmother every day for sweet osmanthus flowers. Later, my mother thought of a toy that she had made in her mother's house when she was a child—making osmanthus candy.

Readers probably have never tasted this special product that is both fragrant and sweet. Now is the time when the trees are covered with flowers, so I will tell you how to make it.

Osmanthus is a kind of small flower, and each flower has a thin stem. The bitter taste that I tasted was the juice of that stem, so when making osmanthus candy, you must remove the stems, but this is the most troublesome task. Because my mother was experienced, she invented the easiest procedure: when the osmanthus flowers are about to wither, spread a single quilt on the ground and shake the tree trunk. The flowers will separate from the flower stems and hang down. Although the yellow leaves and branches of the tree are mixed in, it is much easier than selecting and picking the flower stems.

When the work of selecting and picking the flowers is completed, put them in a ceramic jar, store them with clean water, so that the mud on the flowers will go into the water, use a stone mortar to mash the flowers, and mix them with sugar evenly. If you like almonds. In this way, it becomes a big ball of osmanthus candy like kneading flour.

Although I would grab and eat it at that time, this big ball of stuff cannot be stored for a long time. It has to go through another layer of printing board to make each piece of exquisite osmanthus candy, and then store it in a lime box, wait for the moisture to dry, and the candy can be stored for a long time without spoiling, and the color, aroma, and taste are all excellent.

Printing boards are sold in carving shops. On a rectangular wooden board, various patterns are carved in negative shape, such as pomegranates, double carp, a group of harmony... etc. On top of it, there is a thin cover board with the same area, and a hole is carved according to the outline of the pattern in the place where each pattern is equal. When making candy, wipe the carved wooden board with a wet towel (so that the sugar will not stick), cover it with the cover board, and pick a small piece of sugar and fill it in the empty hole. Each board can probably make four or five pieces. After filling all the empty holes, hold one end of the cover board and gently tap it on the table, and it will become a piece of exquisite osmanthus candy.

My sister is five years older than me, and she can help my mother make osmanthus candy, but she can hardly eat a few pieces. I eat it while doing it. Even after storing it in the lime box, I often secretly grab a few pieces and hide them in my pocket. Even if my grandmother and mother see it, they will smile and say nothing. But my sister pouts and says, "Why is only my younger brother allowed to eat?" She doesn't understand the position of a girl in this society. Now she is the mother of three children. Every autumn, she always remembers her younger brother who likes to eat candy and sends the made osmanthus candy from the post office. In last year's letter, she told me that because she sent a package of osmanthus candy to me, her eldest child cried for most of the day. Do you think it's shameful for an uncle and nephew to grab candy to eat? I replied in her letter: When you helped mother make candy when you were a child, you never

Yearning for the Sea 191

— Qi Yun

"One copper coin, a heart full of sorrow, a copy of 'Marfa'."——Struggling up my tired body on the slightly warm beach, I picked up a seashell and wrote the above words in the sand.

After writing, I lay down again.

With eyes stimulated by the strong sunlight, I stared at the clean jade-blue sky and the clouds chasing each other like playing hide-and-seek. The mood was quiet, and the soul seemed to have entered another pure white paradise.

Over the years, the waves of life have tossed and turned my stable life, drifting, wandering, comforted by the spring breeze of the South, and also loved the invasion of the wind and sand of the North. From the season of peach blossoms and mandarin fish, it turned to the days of chrysanthemums and crabs; then again from the days of chrysanthemums, it turned to the season of peach blossoms. One time after another, the days were woven into a long string, flowing past like flowing water, flowing past——making my golden sweet dreams of childhood shatter, and dissolving my innocence and purity in the bitter taste of the sea of people. Occasionally, stealing a moment of leisure, I use a thousand kinds of complaining and longing words to trace the passing of that old dream.……

So, I turned my eyes to the sky again.——

The clouds were changing: like continuous mountains, also like a flock of sheep on the pasture,……Sometimes, they gather tightly together, and then slowly split apart, and the jade-blue sky shows a smiling face in the cracks.

The sea, under the calm and profound breath, is also changing like the clouds. Rolling its soft waist, when tired, it spurts out a mouthful of white foam.

In bursts, carrying the light breeze of autumn, the waves deliver the sound of the waves, as lovely as "Autumn Lullaby"!

When my eyes were about to take my soul into that pure realm, I opened the book. On the first page, the first paragraph, the first line is written:

"The sea is smiling."

Yes, the sea is always smiling. The bursts of waves may be the sound of laughter.——Although in the vast ocean, the waves are hard.

Thinking of hard work, I felt annoyed; so I threw the book away and closed my tired eyes.

In this way, I lightly sent most of the day into the land of sleep.……

Waking up, the sun had already set to the west.

(——The sea is smiling.)

(I am also smiling.——However, my smile has the flavor of autumn.)

New Song Introduction 192

Fisherman's Tears - Culture/Parents/Children Songs

(1) The small boat floats on the white waves, the father and daughter work hard on the river, only because the family is poor and it is difficult to live, fishing is temporarily used as a career.

(2) The river is dry and there are no fish to catch, and the fishing tax and bad rules cannot be spared. Greedy officials and corrupt officials are as fierce as tigers, and local bullies and gentry collude.

(3) The scorching sun steams people and sweat rains down, the elderly father is exhausted, let's rest in the shade of the willows on the other side of the bank, the father and daughter cry together with tears like hemp.

Art 194

Mao Zhizhong Art Lecture

Hangye (1180) 2:45 PM to 3:30 PM

Lecture Summary (1) Art. The Han and Tang dynasties, with their ingenuity, produced countless creations. The advancement of art was almost beyond reason. However, the Southern and Northern Schools rose and fell with each other. Some excelled in hard work, some won with simplicity, and some stood out on their own. Asking about their origins, they were nothing more than deep cultivation behind closed doors and expressing personal feelings. A History of Chinese Artists of All Dynasties.

The Nightingale Art Society is releasing a new song, "Self-Pity," composed by Mr. Liu Lang. The lyrics are mournful and beautiful, and can even be used as a riddle, making it quite interesting. Simple sheet music with staff notation is being distributed to all sectors. If requesting by mail, please include two cents for postage. The Nightingale Art Society's "Nightingale Song Selection" has a limited number of copies remaining. Mail orders are priced at 15 cents per copy. To facilitate mail orders from both local and out-of-town locations, postage is waived. Send letters to the China Radio Station in the Great World amusement park, or to the Anding Radio Station at 15 Fukang Road, Xinzha Road, or to Room 410, Jin Xing Building, 505 Henan Road, specifying the Nightingale Art Society, to purchase the songbook.

This issue's content is even richer, featuring songs such as "Nie Er's Elegy," "Farewell to Nanyang," "Night-Blooming Jasmine," "Love Song," "Newlywed Sweetness," "Lotus Picking Song," and "Tuberose," among others. It also includes dozens of opening verses of "Mid-Autumn Festival" Suzhou storytelling, as well as "Southern Lyrics of April," "Beautiful Photos," "Cartoons from Various Artists," "Short Essays," "Drama Scripts," "Kunqu Opera," "Poems," "Full-Length Novels," etc. The magazine is sold for 20 cents per copy. An annual subscription is 2.20 yuan. Local postage is an additional 6 cents per year. Postage is free for annual subscribers in other locations when the publication comes out.

Movie News

The First Indian Film "Light of the World" 197

Opening tomorrow at the Garden Cinema

This film is a grand ancient Indian palace romantic musical film with sound. It features real views of a magnificent palace, the majesty of the court, mysterious oriental dances in the palace, tens of thousands of troops and elephants marching into battle, elephant gates, and other features, truly giving it a flavor of another world, rarely seen in other films.

The plot tells the story of a couple who encounter danger in the desert while giving birth to a daughter, who is later rescued. The king, because the father previously rendered meritorious service to the country, specially appointed him as an official and made his daughter his companion. However, when she grew up, because their social statuses were incompatible, the king found a way to send him on an expedition, so that he would be separated from the girl, and secretly married the girl to someone else. The prince was furious when he heard this, betrayed his father, but was eventually captured by his father. The old king died of excessive grief. The new king ascended the throne, welcomed back his lover, and made her the queen. The Garden Cinema is located west of the Cathay Cinema on Avenue Joffre.

Silver Jottings 200

— Zhi Er

In our film industry, there are so-called "writer-stars." Initially, there were the "Three Stage Stars" Ai Xia, Wang Ying, and Hu Ping. Later, we often read articles by "Little Gao" Ping Qian. Now, it seems there are even more. Huang Hou from under Mount Emei, as well as Tong Yue Juan, etc., can all write a piece. And the influence of Ban Hua seems to be gaining momentum in recent days.

A friend came in complaining, saying, "In 'Literary Exchange,' you missed a very famous 'overseas returnee,' Hu Die. Didn't Miss Hu recently write a book about her European tour or something?"

Due to my friend's reminder, I was reminded of the "Eastern Standard Beauty" Xu Lai, who caused a sensation some time ago. Didn't Xu Lai also have something like "100 Days to Becoming a Performer"?

To say that female stars are shallow is truly deserving of a slap on the wrist. Just take the above facts as proof. Aren't our female stars "great" enough? How can they be shallow?

And due to the above facts, I predict that future stars will all be "writer-stars." Even those who are so illiterate that they have to have someone else write their signature will leap forward with this "progressive" trend.
